      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Netbooks">
        Netbooks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Netbooks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Linux distributions have also become popular in the
       <a href="/wiki/Netbook" title="Netbook">
        netbook
       </a>
       market, with many devices such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Asus_Eee_PC" title="Asus Eee PC">
        Asus Eee PC
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspire_One" title="Aspire One">
        Acer Aspire One
       </a>
       shipping with customized Linux distributions installed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2009, Google announced its
       <a href="/wiki/Chrome_OS" title="Chrome OS">
        Chrome OS
       </a>
       as a minimal Linux-based operating system, using the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chrome_browser" title="Chrome browser">
        Chrome browser
       </a>
       as the main user interface. Chrome OS does not run any non-web applications, except for the bundled file manager and media player (a certain level of support for
       <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
        Android
       </a>
       applications was added in later versions).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Netbooks that shipped with the operating system, termed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chromebooks" title="Chromebooks">
        Chromebooks
       </a>
       , started appearing on the market in June 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Servers.2C_mainframes_and_supercomputers">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Servers,_mainframes_and_supercomputers">
        Servers, mainframes and supercomputers
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Servers, mainframes and supercomputers">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LAMP_software_bundle.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1280" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/LAMP_software_bundle.svg/500px-LAMP_software_bundle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/LAMP_software_bundle.svg/750px-LAMP_software_bundle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/LAMP_software_bundle.svg/1000px-LAMP_software_bundle.svg.png 2x" width="500"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LAMP_software_bundle.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Broad overview of the
         <a href="/wiki/LAMP_(software_bundle)" title="LAMP (software bundle)">
          LAMP software bundle
         </a>
         , displayed here together with
         <a href="/wiki/Squid_(software)" title="Squid (software)">
          Squid
         </a>
         . A high-performance and high-availability web server solution providing security in a hostile environment.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_distribution" title="Linux distribution">
        Linux distributions
       </a>
       have long been used as
       <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">
        server
       </a>
       operating systems, and have risen to prominence in that area;
       <a href="/wiki/Netcraft" title="Netcraft">
        Netcraft
       </a>
       reported in September 2006, that eight of the ten (other two with "unknown" OS) most reliable internet hosting companies ran Linux distributions on their
       <a href="/wiki/Web_server" title="Web server">
        web servers
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with Linux in the top position. In June 2008, Linux distributions represented five of the top ten,
       <a href="/wiki/FreeBSD" title="FreeBSD">
        FreeBSD
       </a>
       three of ten, and
       <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">
        Microsoft
       </a>
       two of ten;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       since February 2010, Linux distributions represented six of the top ten, FreeBSD two of ten, and Microsoft one of ten,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with Linux in the top position.
      </p>
      <p>
       Linux distributions are the cornerstone of the
       <a href="/wiki/LAMP_(software_bundle)" title="LAMP (software bundle)">
        LAMP
       </a>
       server-software combination (Linux,
       <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_Server" title="Apache HTTP Server">
        Apache
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/MariaDB" title="MariaDB">
        MariaDB
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">
        MySQL
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">
        Perl
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">
        PHP
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">
        Python
       </a>
       ) which has achieved popularity among developers, and which is one of the more common platforms for website hosting.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SecuritySpace_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SecuritySpace-101">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Linux distributions have become increasingly popular on
       <a href="/wiki/Mainframe_computer" title="Mainframe computer">
        mainframes
       </a>
       , partly due to pricing and the open-source model.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In December 2009, computer giant
       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">
        IBM
       </a>
       reported that it would predominantly market and sell mainframe-based Enterprise Linux Server.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Register_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_Register-103">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LinuxCon" title="LinuxCon">
        LinuxCon North America 2015
       </a>
       , IBM announced
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LinuxONE" title="LinuxONE">
        LinuxONE
       </a>
       , a series of mainframes specifically designed to run Linux and open-source software.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Linux distributions are also dominant as
       <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">
        operating systems
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">
        supercomputers
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_supercomputers_20-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-rules_supercomputers-20">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of November 2017, all supercomputers on the
       <a href="/wiki/TOP500" title="TOP500">
        500
       </a>
       list run some variant of Linux.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-top500stats_106-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-top500stats-106">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Smart_devices">
        Smart devices
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Smart devices">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series_2.jpg/220px-Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series_2.jpg/330px-Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series_2.jpg/440px-Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Android smartphones
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Several operating systems for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smart_devices" title="Smart devices">
        smart devices
       </a>
       , such as
       <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">
        smartphones
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">
        tablet computers
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">
        smart TVs
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-vehicle_infotainment" title="In-vehicle infotainment">
        in-vehicle infotainment
       </a>
       (IVI) systems, are based on Linux. Major platforms for such systems include
       <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
        Android
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Firefox_OS" title="Firefox OS">
        Firefox OS
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mer_(software_distribution)" title="Mer (software distribution)">
        Mer
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tizen" title="Tizen">
        Tizen
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Android has become the dominant mobile operating system for
       <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">
        smartphones
       </a>
       , running on 79.3% of units sold worldwide during the second quarter of 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_107-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-107">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Android is also a popular operating system for tablets, and Android smart TVs and in-vehicle infotainment systems have also appeared in the market.
      </p>
      <p>
       Cellphones and PDAs running Linux on open-source platforms became more common from 2007; examples include the
       <a href="/wiki/Nokia_N810" title="Nokia N810">
        Nokia N810
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Openmoko" title="Openmoko">
        Openmoko
       </a>
       's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo1973" title="Neo1973">
        Neo1973
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorola_ROKR_E8" title="Motorola ROKR E8">
        Motorola ROKR E8
       </a>
       . Continuing the trend,
       <a href="/wiki/Palm,_Inc." title="Palm, Inc.">
        Palm
       </a>
       (later acquired by
       <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">
        HP
       </a>
       ) produced a new Linux-derived operating system,
       <a href="/wiki/WebOS" title="WebOS">
        webOS
       </a>
       , which is built into its line of
       <a href="/wiki/Palm_Pre" title="Palm Pre">
        Palm Pre
       </a>
       smartphones.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
        Nokia
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Maemo" title="Maemo">
        Maemo
       </a>
       , one of the earliest mobile operating systems, was based on
       <a href="/wiki/Debian" title="Debian">
        Debian
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was later merged with
       <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">
        Intel
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Moblin" title="Moblin">
        Moblin
       </a>
       , another Linux-based operating system, to form
       <a href="/wiki/MeeGo" title="MeeGo">
        MeeGo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The project was later terminated in favor of Tizen, an operating system targeted at mobile devices as well as IVI. Tizen is a project within
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Linux_Foundation" title="The Linux Foundation">
        The Linux Foundation
       </a>
       . Several
       <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">
        Samsung
       </a>
       products are already running Tizen,
       <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Gear_2" title="Samsung Gear 2">
        Samsung Gear 2
       </a>
       being the most significant example.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samsung_Z" title="Samsung Z">
        Samsung Z
       </a>
       smartphones will use Tizen instead of Android.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a result of MeeGo's termination, the Mer project forked the MeeGo codebase to create a basis for mobile-oriented operating systems.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In July 2012,
       <a href="/wiki/Jolla" title="Jolla">
        Jolla
       </a>
       announced
       <a href="/wiki/Sailfish_OS" title="Sailfish OS">
        Sailfish OS
       </a>
       , their own mobile operating system built upon Mer technology.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">
        Mozilla's
       </a>
       Firefox OS consists of the Linux kernel, a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hardware_abstraction_layer" title="Hardware abstraction layer">
        hardware abstraction layer
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Web_standards" title="Web standards">
        web-standards
       </a>
       -based
       <a href="/wiki/Runtime_system" title="Runtime system">
        runtime environment
       </a>
       and user interface, and an integrated
       <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">
        web browser
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonical_Ltd." title="Canonical Ltd.">
        Canonical
       </a>
       has released
       <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_Touch" title="Ubuntu Touch">
        Ubuntu Touch
       </a>
       , aiming to bring convergence to the user experience on this mobile operating system and its desktop counterpart,
       <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_(operating_system)" title="Ubuntu (operating system)">
        Ubuntu
       </a>
       . The operating system also provides a full Ubuntu desktop when connected to an external monitor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Embedded_devices">
        Embedded devices
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Embedded devices">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embedded_Linux" title="Embedded Linux">
        Embedded Linux
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linux_devices" title="Linux devices">
        Linux devices
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jolla_smartphones.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jolla_smartphones.jpg/150px-Jolla_smartphones.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jolla_smartphones.jpg/225px-Jolla_smartphones.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jolla_smartphones.jpg/300px-Jolla_smartphones.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jolla_smartphones.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jolla_(mobile_phone)" title="Jolla (mobile phone)">
          Jolla Phone
         </a>
         has the Linux-based
         <a href="/wiki/Sailfish_OS" title="Sailfish OS">
          Sailfish OS
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg/150px-Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg/225px-Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg/300px-Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/In-car_entertainment" title="In-car entertainment">
          In-car entertainment
         </a>
         system of the
         <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
          Tesla Model S
         </a>
         is based on
         <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_(operating_system)" title="Ubuntu (operating system)">
          Ubuntu
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
          <a href="#cite_note-115">
           [113]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:My_green_Nokia_X_(13582469484).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2634" data-file-width="1503" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/My_green_Nokia_X_%2813582469484%29.jpg/150px-My_green_Nokia_X_%2813582469484%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/My_green_Nokia_X_%2813582469484%29.jpg/225px-My_green_Nokia_X_%2813582469484%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/My_green_Nokia_X_%2813582469484%29.jpg/300px-My_green_Nokia_X_%2813582469484%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:My_green_Nokia_X_(13582469484).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Nokia_X" title="Nokia X">
          Nokia X
         </a>
         , a smartphone that runs Linux kernel
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Due to its low cost and ease of customization,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embedded_Linux" title="Embedded Linux">
        Linux
       </a>
       is often used in
       <a href="/wiki/Embedded_system" title="Embedded system">
        embedded systems
       </a>
       . In the non-mobile telecommunications equipment sector, the majority of
       <a href="/wiki/Customer-premises_equipment" title="Customer-premises equipment">
        customer-premises equipment
       </a>
       (CPE) hardware runs some Linux-based operating system.
       <a href="/wiki/OpenWrt" title="OpenWrt">
        OpenWrt
       </a>
       is a community driven example upon which many of the OEM firmware releases are based.
      </p>
      <p>
       For example, the popular
       <a href="/wiki/TiVo" title="TiVo">
        TiVo
       </a>
       digital video recorder also uses a customized Linux,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tivo_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tivo-116">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as do several network
       <a href="/wiki/Firewall_(computing)" title="Firewall (computing)">
        firewalls
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Router_(computing)" title="Router (computing)">
        routers
       </a>
       from such makers as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cisco" title="Cisco">
        Cisco
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Linksys" title="Linksys">
        Linksys
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Korg_OASYS" title="Korg OASYS">
        Korg OASYS
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korg_KRONOS" title="Korg KRONOS">
        Korg KRONOS
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Yamaha_Motif#Motif_XS" title="Yamaha Motif">
        Yamaha Motif XS
       </a>
       /Motif XF
       <a href="/wiki/Music_workstation" title="Music workstation">
        music workstations
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Yamaha S90XS/S70XS, Yamaha MOX6/MOX8 synthesizers, Yamaha Motif-Rack XS
       <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">
        tone generator module
       </a>
       , and Roland RD-700GX
       <a href="/wiki/Digital_piano" title="Digital piano">
        digital piano
       </a>
       also run Linux. Linux is also used in
       <a href="/wiki/Stage_lighting" title="Stage lighting">
        stage lighting
       </a>
       control systems, such as the WholeHogIII console.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gaming">
        Gaming
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Gaming">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_gaming" title="Linux gaming">
        Linux gaming
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the past, not many games were available for Linux, but in the recent years, more games have been released with support for Linux. Nowadays, many games support Linux (especially
       <a href="/wiki/Indie_game" title="Indie game">
        Indie games
       </a>
       ), except for a few
       <a href="/wiki/AAA_(video_game_industry)" title="AAA (video game industry)">
        AAA title
       </a>
       games. On the other hand, as a popular mobile platform,
       <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
        Android
       </a>
       (which uses the
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">
        Linux kernel
       </a>
       ) has gained much developer interest and is one of the main platforms for mobile game development along with
       <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">
        iOS
       </a>
       operating system by
       <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">
        Apple
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">
        iPhone
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">
        iPad
       </a>
       devices.
      </p>
      <p>
       On February 14, 2013,
       <a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">
        Valve
       </a>
       released a Linux version of
       <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" title="Steam (software)">
        Steam
       </a>
       , a popular game distribution platform on PC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many Steam games were ported to Linux.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On December 13, 2013, Valve released
       <a href="/wiki/SteamOS" title="SteamOS">
        SteamOS
       </a>
       , a gaming oriented OS based on Debian, for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beta_testing" title="Beta testing">
        beta testing
       </a>
       , and has plans to ship
       <a href="/wiki/Steam_Machine_(hardware_platform)" title="Steam Machine (hardware platform)">
        Steam Machines
       </a>
       as a gaming and entertainment platform.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Valve has also developed
       <a href="/wiki/VOGL" title="VOGL">
        VOGL
       </a>
       , an
       <a href="/wiki/OpenGL" title="OpenGL">
        OpenGL
       </a>
       debugger intended to aid video game development,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as porting its
       <a href="/wiki/Source_(game_engine)" title="Source (game engine)">
        Source
       </a>
       game engine to desktop Linux.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result of Valve's effort, several prominent games such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Dota_2" title="Dota 2">
         DotA 2
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">
         Team Fortress 2
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Portal_(video_game)" title="Portal (video game)">
         Portal
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Portal_2" title="Portal 2">
         Portal 2
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Left_4_Dead_2" title="Left 4 Dead 2">
         Left 4 Dead 2
        </a>
       </i>
       are now natively available on desktop Linux.
      </p>
      <p>
       On July 31, 2013,
       <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">
        Nvidia
       </a>
       released
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nvidia_Shield" title="Nvidia Shield">
        Shield
       </a>
       as an attempt to use Android as a specialized gaming platform.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some Linux users play Windows games through
       <a href="/wiki/Wine_(software)" title="Wine (software)">
        Wine
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/CrossOver_(software)" title="CrossOver (software)">
        CrossOver Linux
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Specialized_uses">
        Specialized uses
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Specialized uses">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Due to the flexibility, customizability and free and open-source nature of Linux, it becomes possible to highly tune Linux for a specific purpose. There are two main methods for creating a specialized Linux distribution: building from scratch or from a general-purpose distribution as a base. The distributions often used for this purpose include
       <a href="/wiki/Debian" title="Debian">
        Debian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fedora_(operating_system)" title="Fedora (operating system)">
        Fedora
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_(operating_system)" title="Ubuntu (operating system)">
        Ubuntu
       </a>
       (which is itself based on Debian),
       <a href="/wiki/Arch_Linux" title="Arch Linux">
        Arch Linux
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gentoo_Linux" title="Gentoo Linux">
        Gentoo
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Slackware" title="Slackware">
        Slackware
       </a>
       . In contrast, Linux distributions built from scratch do not have general-purpose bases; instead, they focus on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JeOS" title="JeOS">
        JeOS
       </a>
       philosophy by including only necessary components and avoiding
       <a href="/wiki/System_resource" title="System resource">
        resource
       </a>
       overhead caused by components considered redundant in the distribution's use cases.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Home_theater_PC">
        Home theater PC
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Home theater PC">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Home_theater_PC" title="Home theater PC">
        home theater PC
       </a>
       (HTPC) is a PC that is mainly used as an entertainment system, especially a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_theater_system" title="Home theater system">
        Home theater system
       </a>
       . It is normally connected to a television, and often an additional audio system.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/OpenELEC" title="OpenELEC">
        OpenELEC
       </a>
       , a Linux distribution that incorporates the media center software
       <a href="/wiki/Kodi_(software)" title="Kodi (software)">
        Kodi
       </a>
       , is an OS tuned specifically for an HTPC. Having been built from the ground up adhering to the JeOS principle, the OS is very lightweight and very suitable for the confined usage range of an HTPC.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are also special editions of Linux distributions that include the
       <a href="/wiki/MythTV" title="MythTV">
        MythTV
       </a>
       media center software, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Mythbuntu" title="Mythbuntu">
        Mythbuntu
       </a>
       , a special edition of Ubuntu.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_security">
        Digital security
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Digital security">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Kali_Linux" title="Kali Linux">
        Kali Linux
       </a>
       is a Debian-based Linux distribution designed for
       <a href="/wiki/Digital_forensics" title="Digital forensics">
        digital forensics
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Penetration_test" title="Penetration test">
        penetration testing
       </a>
       . It comes preinstalled with several software applications for penetration testing and identifying
       <a href="/wiki/Exploit_(computer_security)" title="Exploit (computer security)">
        security exploits
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Ubuntu derivative
       <a href="/wiki/BackBox" title="BackBox">
        BackBox
       </a>
       provides pre-installed security and network analysis tools for ethical hacking.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are many Linux distributions created with privacy, secrecy, network anonymity and information security in mind, including
       <a href="/wiki/Tails_(operating_system)" title="Tails (operating system)">
        Tails
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tin_Hat_Linux" title="Tin Hat Linux">
        Tin Hat Linux
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tinfoil_Hat_Linux" title="Tinfoil Hat Linux">
        Tinfoil Hat Linux
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Lightweight_Portable_Security" title="Lightweight Portable Security">
        Lightweight Portable Security
       </a>
       is a distribution based on Arch Linux and developed by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">
        United States Department of Defense
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Tor-ramdisk" title="Tor-ramdisk">
        Tor-ramdisk
       </a>
       is a minimal distribution created solely to host the network anonymity software
       <a href="/wiki/Tor_(anonymity_network)" title="Tor (anonymity network)">
        Tor
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="System_rescue">
        System rescue
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: System rescue">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Linux
       <a href="/wiki/Live_CD" title="Live CD">
        Live CD
       </a>
       sessions have long been used as a tool for recovering data from a broken computer system and for repairing the system. Building upon that idea, several Linux distributions tailored for this purpose have emerged, most of which use
       <a href="/wiki/GParted" title="GParted">
        GParted
       </a>
       as a partition editor, with additional data recovery and system repair software:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gparted_live" title="Gparted live">
         GParted Live
        </a>
        –  a Debian-based distribution developed by the GParted project.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Parted_Magic" title="Parted Magic">
         Parted Magic
        </a>
        –  a commercial Linux distribution.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/SystemRescueCD" title="SystemRescueCD">
         SystemRescueCD
        </a>
        –  a Gentoo-based distribution with support for editing Windows
        <a href="/wiki/Windows_Registry" title="Windows Registry">
         registry
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_space">
        In space
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: In space">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">
        SpaceX
       </a>
       uses multiple redundant
       <a href="/wiki/Category:Avionics_computers" title="Category:Avionics computers">
        flight computers
       </a>
       in a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fault-tolerant_design" title="Fault-tolerant design">
        fault-tolerant design
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">
        Falcon 9
       </a>
       rocket. Each Merlin engine is controlled by three
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voting_logic" title="Voting logic">
        voting
       </a>
       computers, with two physical processors per computer that constantly check each other's operation. Linux is not inherently fault-tolerant (no operating system is, as it is a function of the whole system including the hardware), but the flight computer software makes it so for its purpose.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aw20121118_126-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aw20121118-126">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For flexibility,
       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_off-the-shelf" title="Commercial off-the-shelf">
        commercial off-the-shelf
       </a>
       parts and system-wide "radiation-tolerant" design are used instead of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radiation_hardened" title="Radiation hardened">
        radiation hardened
       </a>
       parts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aw20121118_126-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aw20121118-126">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of June 2015
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , SpaceX has made 19 launches of the Falcon 9 since 2010, out of which 18 have successfully delivered their primary payloads to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth_orbit" title="Earth orbit">
        Earth orbit
       </a>
       , including some support missions for the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">
        International Space Station
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition, Windows was used as an operating system on non-mission critical systems‍—‌laptops used on board the space station, for example‍—‌but it has been replaced with Linux; the first Linux-powered humanoid robot is also undergoing in-flight testing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">
        Jet Propulsion Laboratory
       </a>
       has used Linux for a number of years "to help with projects relating to the construction of unmanned space flight and deep space exploration";
       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
        NASA
       </a>
       uses Linux in robotics in the Mars rover, and
       <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_(operating_system)" title="Ubuntu (operating system)">
        Ubuntu
       </a>
       Linux to "save data from satellites".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Linux distributions have been created to provide hands-on experience with coding and source code to students, on devices such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Raspberry_Pi" title="Raspberry Pi">
        Raspberry Pi
       </a>
       . In addition to producing a practical device, the intention is to show students "how things work under the hood".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Ubuntu derivatives
       <a href="/wiki/Edubuntu" title="Edubuntu">
        Edubuntu
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/The_Linux_Schools_Project" title="The Linux Schools Project">
        The Linux Schools Project
       </a>
       , as well as the Debian derivative
       <a href="/wiki/Skolelinux" title="Skolelinux">
        Skolelinux
       </a>
       , provide education-oriented software packages. They also include tools for administering and building school computer labs and computer-based classrooms, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_Terminal_Server_Project" title="Linux Terminal Server Project">
        Linux Terminal Server Project
       </a>
       (LTSP).
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Others">
        Others
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Others">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Instant_WebKiosk" title="Instant WebKiosk">
        Instant WebKiosk
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Webconverger" title="Webconverger">
        Webconverger
       </a>
       are browser-based Linux distributions often used in web
       <a href="/wiki/Interactive_kiosk" title="Interactive kiosk">
        kiosks
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Digital_signage" title="Digital signage">
        digital signage
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Thinstation" title="Thinstation">
        Thinstation
       </a>
       is a minimalist distribution designed for
       <a href="/wiki/Thin_client" title="Thin client">
        thin clients
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Rocks_Cluster_Distribution" title="Rocks Cluster Distribution">
        Rocks Cluster Distribution
       </a>
       is tailored for
       <a href="/wiki/HPCC" title="HPCC">
        high-performance computing clusters
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There are general-purpose Linux distributions that target a specific audience, such as users of a specific language or geographical area. Such examples include
       <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_Kylin" title="Ubuntu Kylin">
        Ubuntu Kylin
       </a>
       for Chinese language users and
       <a href="/wiki/BlankOn" title="BlankOn">
        BlankOn
       </a>
       targeted at Indonesians. Profession-specific distributions include
       <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_Studio" title="Ubuntu Studio">
        Ubuntu Studio
       </a>
       for media creation and
       <a href="/wiki/DNALinux" title="DNALinux">
        DNALinux
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics" title="Bioinformatics">
        bioinformatics
       </a>
       . There is also a Muslim-oriented distribution of the name
       <a href="/wiki/Sabily" title="Sabily">
        Sabily
       </a>
       , as well as an Arabic-focused distribution called
       <a href="/wiki/Ojuba_Linux" title="Ojuba Linux">
        Ojuba Linux
       </a>
       that consequently also provides some Islamic tools. Certain organizations use slightly specialized Linux distributions internally, including
       <a href="/wiki/GendBuntu" title="GendBuntu">
        GendBuntu
       </a>
       used by the French
       <a href="/wiki/National_Gendarmerie" title="National Gendarmerie">
        National Gendarmerie
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Goobuntu" title="Goobuntu">
        Goobuntu
       </a>
       used internally by Google, and
       <a href="/wiki/Astra_Linux" title="Astra Linux">
        Astra Linux
       </a>
       developed specifically for the Russian army.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Market_share_and_uptake">
        Market share and uptake
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Market share and uptake">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_adoption" title="Linux adoption">
        Linux adoption
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Usage_share_of_operating_systems" title="Usage share of operating systems">
        Usage share of operating systems
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many quantitative studies of
       <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">
        free
       </a>
       /open-source software focus on topics including market share and reliability, with numerous studies specifically examining Linux.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Linux market is growing rapidly, and the revenue of servers, desktops, and packaged software running Linux was expected to
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="Expected to? (December 2015)">
           needs update
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       exceed $35.7 billion by 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Analysts and proponents attribute the relative success of Linux to its security, reliability, low cost, and freedom from
       <a href="/wiki/Vendor_lock-in" title="Vendor lock-in">
        vendor lock-in
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Desktops and laptops
       </dt>
       <dd>
        According to
        <a href="/wiki/Web_analytics" title="Web analytics">
         web server statistics
        </a>
        , as of June 2016
        <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit">
          [update]
         </a>
        </sup>
        , the estimated market share of Linux on
        <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">
         desktop computers
        </a>
        is around 1.8%. In comparison,
        <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">
         Microsoft Windows
        </a>
        has a market share of around 89.7%, while
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mac_OS" title="Mac OS">
         Mac OS
        </a>
        covers around 8.5%.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Netmarketshare.com_21-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Netmarketshare.com-21">
          [19]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Web servers
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        W3Cook publishes stats that use the top 1,000,000 Alexa domains,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
         <a href="#cite_note-134">
          [132]
         </a>
        </sup>
        which as of May 2015
        <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit">
          [update]
         </a>
        </sup>
        estimate that 96.55% of web servers run Linux, 1.73% run Windows, and 1.72% run FreeBSD.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
         <a href="#cite_note-135">
          [133]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        W3Techs publishes stats that use the top 10,000,000 Alexa domains, updated monthly
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
         <a href="#cite_note-136">
          [134]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and as of November 2016
        <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit">
          [update]
         </a>
        </sup>
        estimate that 66.7% of web servers run Linux/Unix, and 33.4% run Microsoft Windows.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
         <a href="#cite_note-137">
          [135]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        In September 2008, Microsoft's CEO
        <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ballmer" title="Steve Ballmer">
         Steve Ballmer
        </a>
        stated that 60% of web servers ran Linux, versus 40% that ran
        <a href="/wiki/Windows_Server" title="Windows Server">
         Windows Server
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PC_World_September_2008_138-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-PC_World_September_2008-138">
          [136]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/International_Data_Corporation" title="International Data Corporation">
         IDC
        </a>
        's Q1 2007 report indicated that Linux held 12.7% of the overall server market at that time;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Linux-watch.com_IDC's_Q1_2007_report_139-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Linux-watch.com_IDC's_Q1_2007_report-139">
          [137]
         </a>
        </sup>
        this estimate was based on the number of Linux servers sold by various companies, and did not include server hardware purchased separately that had Linux installed on it later.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Mobile devices
       </dt>
       <dd>
        Android, which is based on the Linux kernel, has become the dominant operating system for
        <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">
         smartphones
        </a>
        . During the second quarter of 2013, 79.3% of smartphones sold worldwide used Android.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_107-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-:0-107">
          [105]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Android is also a popular operating system for tablets, being responsible for more than 60% of tablet sales as of 2013.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
         <a href="#cite_note-140">
          [138]
         </a>
        </sup>
        According to web server statistics, as of December 2014
        <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit">
          [update]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Android has a market share of about 46%, with
        <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">
         iOS
        </a>
        holding 45%, and the remaining 9% attributed to various niche platforms.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
         <a href="#cite_note-141">
          [139]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Film production
       </dt>
       <dd>
        For years Linux has been the platform of choice in the film industry. The first major film produced on Linux servers was 1997's
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">
          Titanic
         </a>
        </i>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
         <a href="#cite_note-142">
          [140]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
         <a href="#cite_note-143">
          [141]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Since then major studios including
        <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">
         DreamWorks Animation
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">
         Pixar
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Weta_Digital" title="Weta Digital">
         Weta Digital
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">
         Industrial Light &amp; Magic
        </a>
        have migrated to Linux.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
         <a href="#cite_note-144">
          [142]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
         <a href="#cite_note-145">
          [143]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
         <a href="#cite_note-146">
          [144]
         </a>
        </sup>
        According to the Linux Movies Group, more than 95% of the servers and desktops at large animation and visual effects companies use Linux.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
         <a href="#cite_note-147">
          [145]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Use in government
       </dt>
       <dd>
        Linux distributions have also gained popularity with various local and national governments. The federal government of Brazil is well known for its support for Linux.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
         <a href="#cite_note-148">
          [146]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
         <a href="#cite_note-149">
          [147]
         </a>
        </sup>
        News of the Russian military creating its own Linux distribution has also surfaced, and has come to fruition as the G.H.ost Project.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
         <a href="#cite_note-150">
          [148]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The Indian state of
        <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">
         Kerala
        </a>
        has gone to the extent of mandating that all state high schools run Linux on their computers.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
         <a href="#cite_note-151">
          [149]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
         <a href="#cite_note-152">
          [150]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">
         China
        </a>
        uses Linux exclusively as the operating system for its
        <a href="/wiki/Loongson" title="Loongson">
         Loongson
        </a>
        processor family to achieve technology independence.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
         <a href="#cite_note-153">
          [151]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In Spain, some regions have developed their own Linux distributions, which are widely used in education and official institutions, like
        <a href="/wiki/GnuLinEx" title="GnuLinEx">
         gnuLinEx
        </a>
        in Extremadura and
        <a href="/wiki/Guadalinex" title="Guadalinex">
         Guadalinex
        </a>
        in Andalusia.
        <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
         France
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
         Germany
        </a>
        have also taken steps toward the adoption of Linux.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
         <a href="#cite_note-154">
          [152]
         </a>
        </sup>
        North Korea's
        <a href="/wiki/Red_Star_OS" title="Red Star OS">
         Red Star OS
        </a>
        , developed since 2002, is based on a version of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fedora_Linux" title="Fedora Linux">
         Fedora Linux
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
         <a href="#cite_note-155">
          [153]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h2>
       <span id="Copyright.2C_trademark_and_naming">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Copyright,_trademark_and_naming">
        Copyright, trademark and naming
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Copyright, trademark and naming">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/GNU/Linux_naming_controversy" title="GNU/Linux naming controversy">
        GNU/Linux naming controversy
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SCO-Linux_controversies" title="SCO-Linux controversies">
        SCO-Linux controversies
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Linux kernel is
       <a href="/wiki/Software_license" title="Software license">
        licensed
       </a>
       under the
       <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">
        GNU General Public License
       </a>
       (GPL), version 2. The GPL requires that anyone who distributes software based on source code under this license, must make the originating source code (and any modifications) available to the recipient under the same terms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
        <a href="#cite_note-156">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other key components of a typical Linux distribution are also mainly licensed under the GPL, but they may use other licenses; many libraries use the
       <a href="/wiki/GNU_Lesser_General_Public_License" title="GNU Lesser General Public License">
        GNU Lesser General Public License
       </a>
       (LGPL), a more permissive variant of the GPL, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X.org_Server" title="X.org Server">
        X.org
       </a>
       implementation of the
       <a href="/wiki/X_Window_System" title="X Window System">
        X Window System
       </a>
       uses the
       <a href="/wiki/MIT_License" title="MIT License">
        MIT License
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Torvalds states that the Linux kernel will not move from version 2 of the GPL to version 3.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He specifically dislikes some provisions in the new license which prohibit the use of the software in
       <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">
        digital rights management
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It would also be impractical to obtain permission from all the copyright holders, who number in the thousands.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2001 study of
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Hat_Linux" title="Red Hat Linux">
        Red Hat Linux
       </a>
       7.1 found that this distribution contained 30 million
       <a href="/wiki/Source_lines_of_code" title="Source lines of code">
        source lines of code
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estimating_size_161-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-estimating_size-161">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Using the
       <a href="/wiki/COCOMO" title="COCOMO">
        Constructive Cost Model
       </a>
       , the study estimated that this distribution required about eight thousand person-years of development time. According to the study, if all this software had been developed by conventional
       <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">
        proprietary
       </a>
       means, it would have cost about $1.53 billion (2018 US dollars) to develop in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estimating_size_161-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-estimating_size-161">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of the source code (71%) was written in the
       <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">
        C
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Computer_programming" title="Computer programming">
        programming
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">
        language
       </a>
       , but many other languages were used, including
       <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">
        C++
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lisp_(programming_language)" title="Lisp (programming language)">
        Lisp
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Assembly_language" title="Assembly language">
        assembly language
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">
        Perl
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">
        Python
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fortran" title="Fortran">
        Fortran
       </a>
       , and various
       <a href="/wiki/Shell_script" title="Shell script">
        shell scripting
       </a>
       languages. Slightly over half of all lines of code were licensed under the GPL. The Linux kernel itself was 2.4 million lines of code, or 8% of the total.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estimating_size_161-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-estimating_size-161">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In a later study, the same analysis was performed for
       <a href="/wiki/Debian" title="Debian">
        Debian
       </a>
       version 4.0 (etch, which was released in 2007).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This distribution contained close to 283 million source lines of code, and the study estimated that it would have required about seventy three thousand man-years and cost US$8.46 billion (in 2018 dollars) to develop by conventional means.
      </p>
      <p>
       <span id="POWDER">
       </span>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LinuxWasch3.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/LinuxWasch3.jpg/220px-LinuxWasch3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/LinuxWasch3.jpg/330px-LinuxWasch3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/LinuxWasch3.jpg/440px-LinuxWasch3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LinuxWasch3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The name "Linux" is also used for a laundry detergent made by Swiss company Rösch.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
          <a href="#cite_note-163">
           [161]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the United States, the name
       <i>
        Linux
       </i>
       is a trademark registered to Linus Torvalds.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_trademark_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-US_trademark-9">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Initially, nobody registered it, but on August 15, 1994, William R. Della Croce, Jr. filed for the trademark
       <i>
        Linux
       </i>
       , and then demanded royalties from Linux distributors. In 1996, Torvalds and some affected organizations sued him to have the trademark assigned to Torvalds, and, in 1997, the case was settled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The licensing of the trademark has since been handled by the
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_Mark_Institute" title="Linux Mark Institute">
        Linux Mark Institute
       </a>
       (LMI). Torvalds has stated that he trademarked the name only to prevent someone else from using it. LMI originally charged a nominal sublicensing fee for use of the Linux name as part of trademarks,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
        <a href="#cite_note-165">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but later changed this in favor of offering a free, perpetual worldwide sublicense.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
        <a href="#cite_note-166">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">
        Free Software Foundation
       </a>
       (FSF) prefers
       <i>
        GNU/Linux
       </i>
       as the name when referring to the operating system as a whole, because it considers Linux distributions to be
       <a href="/wiki/GNU_variants" title="GNU variants">
        variants
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/GNU" title="GNU">
        GNU
       </a>
       operating system initiated in 1983 by
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stallman" title="Richard Stallman">
        Richard Stallman
       </a>
       , president of the FSF.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnu_linux_faq_31-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gnu_linux_faq-31">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-linux-and-gnu_32-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-linux-and-gnu-32">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They explicitly take no issue over the name Android for the Android OS, which is also an operating system based on the Linux kernel, as GNU is not a part of it.
      </p>
      <p>
       A minority of public figures and software projects other than Stallman and the FSF, notably
       <a href="/wiki/Debian" title="Debian">
        Debian
       </a>
       (which had been sponsored by the FSF up to 1996),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
        <a href="#cite_note-167">
         [165]
        </a>
       </sup>
       also use
       <i>
        GNU/Linux
       </i>
       when referring to the operating system as a whole.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tivo_116-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-tivo-116">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         [166]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
        <a href="#cite_note-169">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most media and common usage, however, refers to this family of operating systems simply as
       <i>
        Linux
       </i>
       , as do many large Linux distributions (for example,
       <a href="/wiki/SUSE_Linux" title="SUSE Linux">
        SUSE Linux
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Hat_Enterprise_Linux" title="Red Hat Enterprise Linux">
        Red Hat Enterprise Linux
       </a>
       ). By contrast, Linux distributions containing only free software use "GNU/Linux" or simply "GNU", such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trisquel_GNU/Linux" title="Trisquel GNU/Linux">
        Trisquel GNU/Linux
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Parabola_GNU/Linux-libre" title="Parabola GNU/Linux-libre">
        Parabola GNU/Linux-libre
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/BLAG_Linux_and_GNU" title="BLAG Linux and GNU">
        BLAG Linux and GNU
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/GNewSense" title="GNewSense">
        gNewSense
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As of May 2011
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , about 8% to 13% of a modern Linux distribution is made of GNU components (the range depending on whether
       <a href="/wiki/GNOME" title="GNOME">
        GNOME
       </a>
       is considered part of GNU), as determined by counting
       <a href="/wiki/Source_lines_of_code" title="Source lines of code">
        lines of source code
       </a>
       making up Ubuntu's "Natty" release; meanwhile, 6% is taken by the Linux kernel, increased to 9% when including its direct dependencies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-how-much-gnu_170-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-how-much-gnu-170">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">

        <li style="display:table-row">
         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">

         </span>
         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portal:Free_software" title="Portal:Free software">
           Free software portal
          </a>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li style="display:table-row">
         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NewTux.svg">
           <img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="625" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/NewTux.svg/23px-NewTux.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/NewTux.svg/35px-NewTux.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/NewTux.svg/47px-NewTux.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle">
          <a href="/wiki/Portal:Linux" title="Portal:Linux">
           Linux portal
          </a>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li style="display:table-row">
         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">
          <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="28" data-file-width="32" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/32px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/48px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/64px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png 2x" width="32"/>
         </span>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Linux&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-7">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-7">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           GNU is the primary userland used in nearly all Linux distros.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
            <a href="#cite_note-2">
             [2]
            </a>
           </sup>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
            <a href="#cite_note-3">
             [3]
            </a>
           </sup>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
            <a href="#cite_note-4">
             [4]
            </a>
           </sup>
           The GNU userland contains system daemons, user applications, the GUI, and various libraries.
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GNU_Coreutils" title="GNU Coreutils">
            GNU Core utilities
           </a>
           are an essential part of most distros. Most Linux distributions use the
           <a href="/wiki/X_Window_System" title="X Window System">
            X Window
           </a>
           system.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
            <a href="#cite_note-5">
             [5]
            </a>
           </sup>
           Other components of the userland, such as the
           <a href="/wiki/Widget_toolkit" title="Widget toolkit">
            widget toolkit
           </a>
           , vary with the specific distribution, desktop environment, and user configuration.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
            <a href="#cite_note-6">
             [6]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-10">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-10">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           "Linux" trademark is owned by
           <a href="/wiki/Linus_Torvalds" title="Linus Torvalds">
            Linus Torvalds
           </a>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_trademark_9-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-US_trademark-9">
             [8]
            </a>
           </sup>
           and administered by the
           <a href="/wiki/Linux_Mark_Institute" title="Linux Mark Institute">
            Linux Mark Institute
           </a>
           .
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-13">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation book">
            Eckert, Jason W. (2012).
            <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=EHLH4S78LmsC&amp;pg=PA33" rel="nofollow">
             <i>
              Linux+ Guide to Linux Certification
             </i>
            </a>
            (Third ed.). Boston, Massachusetts: Cengage Learning. p. 33.
            <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
             ISBN
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1111541538" title="Special:BookSources/978-1111541538">
             978-1111541538
            </a>
            .
            <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130509031220/http://books.google.com/books?id=EHLH4S78LmsC&amp;pg=PA33" rel="nofollow">
             Archived
            </a>
            from the original on May 9, 2013
            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              April 14,
             </span>
             2013
            </span>
            .
            <q>
             The shared commonality of the kernel is what defines a system's membership in the Linux family; the differing
             <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">
              OSS
             </a>
             applications that can interact with the common kernel are what differentiate
             <a href="/wiki/Linux_distribution" title="Linux distribution">
              Linux distributions
             </a>
             .
            </q>

           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=What+would+you+like+to+see+most+in+minix%3F&amp;rft.pub=comp.os.minix&amp;rft_id=news%3A1991Aug25.205708.9541%40klaava.Helsinki.FI&amp;rft.aulast=Torvalds&amp;rft.aufirst=Linus&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fgroups.google.com%2Fgroup%2Fcomp.os.minix%2Fmsg%2Fb813d52cbc5a044b&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALinux">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-42">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-42">
             ^

          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation newsgroup">
            Linus Torvalds (October 14, 1992).
            <a class="external text" href="https://groups.google.com/group/comp.os.linux/msg/4ae6db18d3f49b0e" rel="nofollow">
             "Chicken and egg: How was the first linux gcc binary created??"
            </a>
            .
            <a href="/wiki/Usenet_newsgroup" title="Usenet newsgroup">
             Newsgroup
            </a>
            :
            <a class="external text" href="news:comp.os.minix" rel="nofollow">
             comp.os.minix
            </a>
            .
            <a href="/wiki/Usenet" title="Usenet">
             Usenet:
            </a>
            <a class="external text" href="news:1992Oct12.100843.26287@klaava.Helsinki.FI" rel="nofollow">
             1992Oct12.100843.26287@klaava.Helsinki.FI
            </a>

             </span>

           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Chicken+and+egg%3A+How+was+the+first+linux+gcc+binary+created%3F%3F&amp;rft.pub=comp.os.minix&amp;rft.date=1992-10-14&amp;rft_id=news%3A1992Oct12.100843.26287%40klaava.Helsinki.FI&amp;rft.au=Linus+Torvalds&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fgroups.google.com%2Fgroup%2Fcomp.os.linux%2Fmsg%2F4ae6db18d3f49b0e&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALinux">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-43">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-43">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a href="/wiki/Linus_Torvalds" title="Linus Torvalds">
             Torvalds, Linus
            </a>
            (January 5, 1992).
            <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070819045030/http://www.kernel.org/pub/linux/kernel/Historic/old-versions/RELNOTES-0.12" rel="nofollow">
             "Release notes for Linux v0.12"
            </a>
            . Linux Kernel Archives. Archived from
            <a class="external text" href="https://www.kernel.org/pub/linux/kernel/Historic/old-versions/RELNOTES-0.12" rel="nofollow">
             the original
            </a>
            on August 19, 2007
            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              July 23,
             </span>
             2007
            </span>
            .
            <q>
             The Linux copyright will change: I've had a couple of requests to make it compatible with the GNU copyleft, removing the “you may not distribute it for money” condition. I agree. I propose that the copyright be changed so that it confirms to GNU ─ pending approval of the persons who have helped write code. I assume this is going to be no problem for anybody: If you have grievances ("I wrote that code assuming the copyright would stay the same") mail me. Otherwise The GNU copyleft takes effect since the first of February. If you do not know the gist of the GNU copyright ─ read it.
            </q>
           </cite>

            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>

             ...we have tried to use the word "Linux" or the expression "Linux kernel" to designate the kernel, and GNU/Linux to designate the entire body of GNU/GPL'ed OS software,... ...many people forget that the linux kernel mailing list is a forum for discussion of kernel-related matters, not GNU/Linux in general...
